### Immediate Action: Employee Assistance on Quantum Computing
Given no current investment actions, I will focus on assisting Emily’s request for a **quantum computing tutorial**. I will provide a concise yet comprehensive beginner-friendly overview covering her specified topics.

---

#### Quantum Computing Tutorial for Emily

**1. Quantum Bits (Qubits) and Superposition**  
- A **classical bit** in traditional computing is binary: it can be either `0` or `1`.  
- A **qubit**, however, can exist in a **superposition** of both 0 and 1, enabling it to perform multiple calculations at once.  
  - **Example/Analogy**: Think of a qubit as a spinning coin. Instead of being "heads" or "tails," it is both until observed.

**2. Quantum Gates and Circuits**  
- Quantum gates manipulate qubits, much like logical gates manipulate classical bits.
  - Example Gates:
    - **Hadamard Gate (H)**: Creates superposition by flipping a qubit.
    - **CNOT Gate**: Entangles two qubits, linking their behavior.
  - Quantum circuits combine gates to perform calculations.

**3. Quantum Entanglement & Teleportation**  
- **Entanglement**: Quantum particles become linked, meaning the state of one instantly influences the other—even at vast distances.
  - Analogy: Imagine a pair of gloves—if you find a left glove, you instantly know the other is a right glove.
- **Teleportation**: Not physical teleportation, but the transfer of quantum states between particles using entanglement.

**4. Quantum Algorithms (e.g., Shor’s, Grover’s)**  
- **Shor’s Algorithm**: Efficiently factors large numbers, breaking traditional encryption methods (e.g., RSA).  
- **Grover’s Algorithm**: Speeds up database searches by leveraging superposition.  
  - Impact: These algorithms showcase quantum computing's transformative potential in fields like cryptography and information retrieval.

**5. Potential Applications in Healthcare and Drug Discovery**
- **Healthcare**: Quantum simulations accelerate understanding of molecular interactions, aiding drug design.
  - **Example**: Modeling how a new drug binds to a protein.
- **Optimization**: Plans radiotherapy schedules or matches patients to clinical trials.

**6. Current Limitations and Challenges**  
- **Hardware Stability**: Quantum systems are sensitive to external noise, leading to high error rates (called **decoherence**).  
- **Scalability**: Building more qubits that can operate reliably is a major hurdle.  
- **Practical Use Cases**: While promising, real-world quantum applications remain in development.

---

### Recommendation to Emily
Emily should explore beginner-friendly resources like:
1. IBM's **Qiskit tutorials** for hands-on quantum programming simulations.
2. Books like "*Quantum Computing for the Very Curious*" by Andy Matuschak.
3. Platforms such as Google's TensorFlow Quantum for novice-friendly experimentation.

### Step 3: Employee Support for Nathan:
Nathan is optimizing the **OCaml-based order matching engine** to reduce garbage collection (GC) impact without sacrificing type safety.

#### Recommendation:
1. **Option 2**: *Multicore OCaml's lock-free data structures*:
   - Use lock-free, non-blocking algorithms to process orders in parallel without the overhead of frequent synchronization or GC interruptions.
   - Multicore OCaml natively supports concurrency, improving throughput for high-volume trading.

2. **Hybrid Approach** with **Pool Allocation for Hot Paths**:
   - Combine lock-free structures with custom memory pools for frequently used paths.
   - Mutable arrays can store cached objects, further reducing GC churn.

This will strike a balance between minimizing GC impact and maintaining the type safety inherent to OCaml.

### Step: Employee Support for James
Now, I’ll turn my attention to helping James optimize his **reinforcement learning portfolio model** for position sizing and rebalancing.

---

### Recommendation for James:
#### 1. **Reward Function Metric**:
- Use **Sortino Ratio** over Sharpe Ratio:
  - Focuses on **downside risk**, which better aligns with portfolio management and avoids penalizing upside volatility.
  - Reward function setup:
    ```
    reward = (returns.mean() - risk_free_rate) / negative_returns.std() - tc_penalty * turnover
    ```

#### 2. **Transaction Cost Modeling**:
- Add a scaling factor to amplify penalties for excessive turnover:
  ```
  tc_penalty = fixed_costs + (dynamic_costs * turnover)
  reward -= tc_penalty
  ```
- Model transaction costs dynamically, scaling penalties with higher turnover rates.

#### Recommendations for Sarah:
1. **Term Structure Modeling**:
   - Transition to **Nelson-Siegel-Svensson (NSS)** for term structure calibration:
     - Better tail behavior and fit for backwardation.
     - Reduces noise in the roll yield estimation.
   - Use rolling **3-month contracts** for illiquid markets to smooth term structure inputs.

2. **Optimal Roll Timing**:
   - Time rolls during **intraday liquidity peaks** (e.g., market opens/near closing auctions).
   - Split larger roll orders into **smaller tranches** to avoid spiking basis risk.

3. **Calendar Spread Arbitrage**:
   - Use **spread options** for arbitrage opportunities to efficiently capture anomalies without executing both legs immediately.

---

#### Recommendations for David:
1. **Reduce Market Impact**:
